cluster. This client also interacts with the broker to allow groups of\n    57→ * consumers to load balance consumption using <a href=\"#consumergroups\">consumer groups</a>.\n    58→ * <p>\n    59→ * The consumer maintains TCP connections to the necessary brokers to fetch data.\n    60→ * Failure to close the consumer after use will leak these connections.\n    61→ * The consumer is not thread-safe. See <a href=\"#multithreaded\">Multi-threaded Processing</a> for more details.\n    62→ *\n    63→ * <h3>Cross-Version Compatibility</h3>\n    64→ * This client can communicate with brokers that are version 0.10.0 or newer. Older or newer brokers may not support\n    65→ * certain features. For example, 0.10.0 brokers do not support offsetsForTimes, because this feature was added\n    66→ * in version 0.10.1. You will receive an {@link org.apache.kafka.common.errors.UnsupportedVersionException}\n    67→ * when invoking an API that is not available on the running broker version.\n    68→ * <p>\n    69→ *\n    70→ * <h3>Offsets and Consumer Position</h3>\n    71→ * Kafka maintains a numerical offset for each record in a partition. This offset acts as a unique identifier of\n    72→ * a record within that partition, and also denotes the position of the consumer in the partition. For example, a consumer\n    73→ * which is at position 5 has consumed records with offsets 0 through 4 and will next receive the record with offset 5.\n    74→ * Note that offsets are not guaranteed to be consecutive (such as compacted topic or when records have been produced\n    75→ * using transactions). For example, if the consumer did read a record with offset 4, but 5 is not an offset\n    76→ * with a record, its position might advance to 6 (or higher) directly. Similarly, if the consumer's position is 5,\n    77→ * but there is no record with offset 5, the consumer will return the record with the next higher offset.\n    78→ * There are actually two notions of position relevant to the user of the consumer:\n    79→ * <p>\n    80→ * The {@link #position(TopicPartition) position} of the consumer gives the offset of the next record that will be given\n    81→ * out. It will be one larger than the highest offset the consumer has seen in that partition. It automatically advances\n    82→ * every time the consumer receives messages in a call to {@link #poll(Duration)}.\n    83→ * <p>\n    84→ * The {@link #commitSync() committed position} is the last offset that has been stored securely. Should the\n    85→ * process fail and restart, this is the offset that the consumer will recover to. The consumer can either automatically commit\n    86→ * offsets periodically; or it can choose to control this committed position manually by calling one of the commit APIs\n    87→ * (e.g. {@link #commitSync() commitSync} and {@link #commitAsync(OffsetCommitCallback) commitAsync}).\n    88→ * <p>\n    89→ * This distinction gives the consumer control over when a record is considered consumed. It is discussed in further\n    90→ * detail below.\n    91→ *\n    92→ * <h3><a name=\"consumergroups\">Consumer Groups and Topic Subscriptions</a></h3>\n    93→ *\n    94→ * Kafka uses the concept of <i>consumer groups</i> to allow a pool of processes to divide the work of consuming and\n    95→ * processing records. These processes can either be running on the same machine or they can be\n    96→ * distributed over many machines to provide scalability and fault tolerance for processing. org.apache.kafka.common.utils.Utils.propsToMap;\n\n/**\n * A client that consumes records from a Kafka cluster.\n * <p>\n * This client transparently handles the failure of Kafka brokers, and transparently adapts as topic partitions\n * it fetches migrate within the cluster. This client also interacts with the broker to allow groups of\n * consumers to load balance consumption using <a href=\"#consumergroups\">consumer groups</a>.\n * <p>\n * The consumer maintains TCP connections to the necessary brokers to fetch data.\n * Failure to close the consumer after use will leak these connections.\n * The consumer is not thread-safe. See <a href=\"#multithreaded\">Multi-threaded Processing</a> for more details.\n *\n * <h3>Cross-Version Compatibility</h3>\n * This client can communicate with brokers that are version 0.10.0 or newer. Older or newer brokers may not support\n * certain features. For example, 0.10.0 brokers do not support offsetsForTimes, because this feature was added\n * in version 0.10.1. You will receive an {@link org.apache.kafka.common.errors.UnsupportedVersionException}\n * when invoking an API that is not available on the running broker version.\n * <p>\n *\n * <h3>Offsets and Consumer Position</h3>\n * Kafka maintains a numerical offset for each record in a partition. This offset acts as a unique identifier of\n * a record within that partition, and also denotes the position of the consumer in the partition. For example, a consumer\n * which is at position 5 has consumed records with offsets 0 through 4 and will next receive the record with offset 5.\n * Note that offsets are not guaranteed to be consecutive (such as compacted topic or when records have been produced\n * using transactions). For example, if the consumer did read a record with offset 4, but 5 is not an offset\n * with a record, its position might advance to 6 (or higher) directly. Similarly, if the consumer's position is 5,\n * but there is no record with offset 5, the consumer will return the record with the next higher offset.\n * There are actually two notions of position relevant to the user of the consumer:\n * <p>\n * The {@link #position(TopicPartition) position} of the consumer gives the offset of the next record that will be given\n * out. It will be one larger than the highest offset the consumer has seen in that partition. It automatically advances\n * every time the consumer receives messages in a call to {@link #poll(Duration)}.\n * <p>\n * The {@link #commitSync() committed position} is the last offset that has been stored securely. Should the\n * process fail and restart, this is the offset that the consumer will recover to. The consumer can either automatically commit\n * offsets periodically; or it can choose to control this committed position manually by calling one of the commit APIs\n * (e.g. {@link #commitSync() commitSync} and {@link #commitAsync(OffsetCommitCallback) commitAsync}).\n * <p>\n * This distinction gives the consumer control over when a record is considered consumed. It is discussed in further\n * detail below.\n *\n * <h3><a name=\"consumergroups\">Consumer Groups and Topic Subscriptions</a></h3>\n *\n * Kafka uses the concept of <i>consumer groups</i> to allow a pool of processes to divide the work of consuming and\n * processing records. These processes can either be running on the same machine or they can be\n * distributed over many machines to provide scalability and fault tolerance for processing. All consumer instances\n * sharing the same {@code group.id} will be part of the same consumer group.\n * <p>\n * Each consumer in a group can dynamically set the list of topics it wants to subscribe to through one of the\n * {@link #subscribe(Collection, ConsumerRebalanceListener) subscribe} APIs.
